          "text": "Now I have a comprehensive understanding of the architecture. Let me summarize what I've found:\n\n## Current Architecture\n\n### Two distinct URLs are hardcoded:\n\n1. **`PRODUCTION_ROO_CODE_API_URL`** = `\"https://app.roocode.com\"` - Used for the Cloud API (auth, settings, share, telemetry, billing). Defined in `packages/cloud/src/config.ts` via `getRooCodeApiUrl()`. Currently reads from `process.env.ROO_CODE_API_URL`.\n\n2. **`ROO_CODE_PROVIDER_URL`** default = `\"https://api.roocode.com/proxy\"` - Used for the Roo provider (model proxy). Currently read from `process.env.ROO_CODE_PROVIDER_URL` in multiple places.\n\n### Where these URLs are used:\n\n**`getRooCodeApiUrl()`** (from `packages/cloud/src/config.ts`):\n- `packages/cloud/src/CloudAPI.ts` - CloudAPI class constructor\n- `packages/cloud/src/CloudSettingsService.ts` - extension settings fetch\n- `packages/cloud/src/WebAuthService.ts` - auth service\n- `src/core/webview/ClineProvider.ts` - passes `cloudApiUrl` to webview state\n- `src/services/marketplace/RemoteConfigLoader.ts` - marketplace config\n\n**`process.env.ROO_CODE_PROVIDER_URL ?? \"https://api.roocode.com/proxy\"`**:\n- `src/api/providers/roo.ts` - Roo provider handler\n- `src/api/providers/fetchers/modelCache.ts` - model cache refresh\n- `src/core/webview/webviewMessageHandler.ts` - two places (roo provider setup)\n- `src/extension/api.ts` - API handler\n- `src/extension.ts` - auth state changed handler\n\n### How VS Code settings work (pattern from `networkProxy.ts`):\n```typescript\nconst config = vscode.workspace.getConfiguration(Package.name)\nconst enabled = Boolean(config.get<unknown>(\"debugProxy.enabled\"))\n```\n\nSettings are defined in `src/package.json` under `contributes.configuration.properties` with the `roo-cline.` prefix.\n\n### Plan:\n\nThe user wants to make the Roo Cloud URL configurable from the VS Code extension settings instead of relying solely on environment variables. Here's my plan:\n\n1. **Add VS Code configuration settings** in `src/package.json`:\n   - `roo-cline.cloudApiUrl` - for the Cloud API URL (default: `\"https://app.roocode.com\"`)\n   - `roo-cline.cloudProviderUrl` - for the Roo provider/proxy URL (default: `\"https://api.roocode.com/proxy\"`)\n\n2. **Add NLS descriptions** in all `src/package.nls*.json` files.\n\n3. **Modify `packages/cloud/src/config.ts`** to accept a configurable URL getter function that can be set from the extension side.\n\n4. **Create a utility in `src/`** that reads the VS Code configuration and provides the URLs, similar to how `networkProxy.ts` reads proxy settings.\n\n5. **Update all references** to use the configurable values instead of hardcoded defaults.\n\n6. **Update the webview** to reflect the configurable URL.\n\nWait, let me reconsider. The `packages/cloud` package is a separate package that doesn't have access to `vscode` directly (it uses `importVscode()` dynamically). This allows\n _ users to point the extension at a self-hosted or development Cloud API,\n _ Provider, and/or Clerk instance.\n _\n _ The VS Code settings are:\n _ - `roo-cline.cloudApiUrl` → overrides `ROO_CODE_API_URL`\n _ - `roo-cline.cloudProviderUrl` → overrides `ROO_CODE_PROVIDER_URL`\n _ - `roo-cline.clerkBaseUrl` → overrides `CLERK_BASE_URL`\n _\n _ Empty strings are treated as \"not set\" so the defaults still apply.\n _/\n\nimport \* as vscode from \"vscode\"\n\nimport { setRooCodeApiUrl, setRooCodeProviderUrl, setClerkBaseUrl } from \"@roo-code/cloud\"\n\nimport { Package } from \"./package\"\n\n/\*\*\n _ Read the current VS Code configuration values and push them into the\n _ `@roo-code/cloud` runtime overrides. This allows\n _ users to point the extension at a self-hosted or development Cloud API,\n _ Provider, and/or Clerk instance.\n _\n _ The VS Code settings are:\n _ - `roo-cline.cloudApiUrl` → overrides `ROO_CODE_API_URL`\n _ - `roo-cline.cloudProviderUrl` → overrides `ROO_CODE_PROVIDER_URL`\n _ - `roo-cline.clerkBaseUrl` → overrides `CLERK_BASE_URL`\n _\n _ Empty strings are treated as \"not set\" so the defaults still apply.\n _/\n\nimport _ as vscode from \"vscode\"\n\nimport { setRooCodeApiUrl, setRooCodeProviderUrl, setClerkBaseUrl } from \"@roo-code/cloud\"\n\nimport { Package } from \"./package\"\n\n/\*\*\n _ Read the current VS Code configuration values and push them into the\n _ `@roo-code/cloud` runtime overrides. Call this once during activation\n _ and again whenever the configuration changes.\n _/\nexport function syncCloudUrls(): void {\n\tconst config = vscode.workspace.getConfiguration(Package.name)\n\n\tconst cloudApiUrl = config.get<string>(\"cloudApiUrl\")?.trim() || undefined\n\tconst cloudProviderUrl = config.get<string>(\"cloudProviderUrl\")?.trim() || undefined\n\tconst clerkBaseUrl = config.get<string>(\"clerkBaseUrl\")?.trim() || undefined\n\n\tsetRooCodeApiUrl(cloudApiUrl)\n\tsetRooCodeProviderUrl(cloudProviderUrl)\n\tsetClerkBaseUrl(clerkBaseUrl)\n}\n\n/\*\*\n _ Register a VS Code configuration-change listener that keeps the cloud URL\n _ overrides in sync whenever the user changes a setting.\n _\n _ Returns a disposable that should be added to `context.subscriptions`.\n _/\nexport function registerCloudUrlsSubscription(context: vscode.ExtensionContext): void {\n\tcontext.subscriptions.push(\n\t\tvscode.workspace.onDidChangeConfiguration((e) => {\n\t\t\tif (\n\t\t\t\te.affectsConfiguration(`${Package.name}.cloudApiUrl`) ||\n\t\t\t\te.affectsConfiguration(`${Package.name}.cloudProviderUrl`) ||\n\t\t\t\te.affectsConfiguration(`${Package.name}.clerkBaseUrl`)\n\t\t\t) {\n\t\t\t\tsyncCloudUrls()\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}),\n\t)\n}"
